"Here's the result of running `cat -n` on /workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/doc.go:\n     1\t/*\n     2\tCopyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\n     3\t\n     4\tLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n     5\tyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n     6\tYou may obtain a copy of the License at\n     7\t\n     8\t    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n     9\t\n    10\tUnless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n    11\tdistributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n    12\tWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n    13\tSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n    14\tlimitations under the License.\n    15\t*/\n    16\t\n    17\t// Package queueset implements a technique called \"fair queuing for\n    18\t// server requests\".  One QueueSet is a set of queues operating\n    19\t// according to this technique.\n    20\t//\n    21\t// Fair queuing for server requests is inspired by the fair queuing\n    22\t// technique from the world of networking.  You can find a good paper\n    23\t// on that at https://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?doid=75247.75248 or\n    24\t// http://people.csail.mit.edu/imcgraw/links/research/pubs/networks/WFQ.pdf\n    25\t// and there is an implementation outline in the Wikipedia article at\n    26\t// https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_queuing .\n    27\t//\n    28\t// Fair queuing for server requests differs from traditional fair\n    29\t// queuing in three ways: (1) we are dispatching application layer\n    30\t// requests to a server rather than transmitting packets on a network\n    31\t// link, (2) multiple requests can be executing at once, and (3) the\n    32\t// service time (execution duration) is not known until the execution\n    33\t// completes.\n    34\t//\n    35\t// The first two differences can easily be handled by straightforward\n    36\t// adaptation of the concept called \"R(t)\" in the original paper and\n    37\t// \"virtual time\" in the implementation outline. In that\n    38\t// implementation outline, the notation now() is used to mean reading\n    39\t// the virtual clock. In the original paper\u2019s terms, \"R(t)\" is the\n    40\t// number of \"rounds\" that have been completed at real time t ---\n    41\t// where a round consists of virtually transmitting one bit from every\n    42\t// non-empty queue in the router (regardless of which queue holds the\n    43\t// packet that is really being transmitted at the moment); in this\n    44\t// conception, a packet is considered to be \"in\" its queue until the\n    45\t// packet\u2019s transmission is finished. For our problem, we can define a\n    46\t// round to be giving one nanosecond of CPU to every non-empty queue\n    47\t// in the apiserver (where emptiness is judged based on both queued\n    48\t// and executing requests from that queue), and define R(t) = (server\n    49\t// start time) + (1 ns) * (number of rounds since server start). Let\n    50\t// us write NEQ(t) for that number of non-empty queues in the\n    51\t// apiserver at time t.  Let us also write C for the concurrency\n    52\t// limit.  In the original paper, the partial derivative of R(t) with\n    53\t// respect to t is\n    54\t//\n    55\t//\t1 / NEQ(t) .\n    56\t//\n    57\t// To generalize from transmitting one packet at a time to executing C\n    58\t// requests at a time, that derivative becomes\n    59\t//\n    60\t//\tC / NEQ(t) .\n    61\t//\n    62\t// However, sometimes there are fewer than C requests available to\n    63\t// execute.  For a given queue \"q\", let us also write \"reqs(q, t)\" for\n    64\t// the number of requests of that queue that are executing at that\n    65\t// time.  The total number of requests executing is sum[over q]\n    66\t// reqs(q, t) and if that is less than C then virtual time is not\n    67\t// advancing as fast as it would if all C seats were occupied; in this\n    68\t// case the numerator of the quotient in that derivative should be\n    69\t// adjusted proportionally.  Putting it all together for fair queing\n    70\t// for server requests: at a particular time t, the partial derivative\n    71\t// of R(t) with respect to t is\n    72\t//\n    73\t//\tmin( C, sum[over q] reqs(q, t) ) / NEQ(t) .\n    74\t//\n    75\t// In terms of the implementation outline, this is the rate at which\n    76\t// virtual time is advancing at time t (in virtual nanoseconds per\n    77\t// real nanosecond). Where the networking implementation outline adds\n    78\t// packet size to a virtual time, in our version this corresponds to\n    79\t// adding a service time (i.e., duration) to virtual time.\n    80\t//\n    81\t// The third difference is handled by modifying the algorithm to\n    82\t// dispatch based on an initial guess at the request\u2019s service time\n    83\t// (duration) and then make the corresponding adjustments once the\n    84\t// request\u2019s actual service time is known. This is similar, although\n    85\t// not exactly isomorphic, to the original paper\u2019s adjustment by\n    86\t// `$\\delta$` for the sake of promptness.\n    87\t//\n    88\t// For implementation simplicity (see below), let us use the same\n    89\t// initial service time guess for every request; call that duration\n    90\t// G. A good choice might be the service time limit (1\n    91\t// minute). Different guesses will give slightly different dynamics,\n    92\t// but any positive number can be used for G without ruining the\n    93\t// long-term behavior.\n    94\t//\n    95\t// As in ordinary fair queuing, there is a bound on divergence from\n    96\t// the ideal. In plain fair queuing the bound is one packet; in our\n    97\t// version it is C requests.\n    98\t//\n    99\t// To support efficiently making the necessary adjustments once a\n   100\t// request\u2019s actual service time is known, the virtual finish time of\n   101\t// a request and the last virtual finish time of a queue are not\n   102\t// represented directly but instead computed from queue length,\n   103\t// request position in the queue, and an alternate state variable that\n   104\t// holds the queue\u2019s virtual start time. While the queue is empty and\n   105\t// has no requests executing: the value of its virtual start time\n   106\t// variable is ignored and its last virtual finish time is considered\n   107\t// to be in the virtual past. When a request arrives to an empty queue\n   108\t// with no requests executing, the queue\u2019s virtual start time is set\n   109\t// to the current virtual time. The virtual finish time of request\n   110\t// number J in the queue (counting from J=1 for the head) is J * G +\n   111\t// (queue's virtual start time). While the queue is non-empty: the\n   112\t// last virtual finish time of the queue is the virtual finish time of\n   113\t// the last request in the queue. While the queue is empty and has a\n   114\t// request executing: the last virtual finish time is the queue\u2019s\n   115\t// virtual start time. When a request is dequeued for service the\n   116\t// queue\u2019s virtual start time is advanced by G. When a request\n   117\t// finishes being served, and the actual service time was S, the\n   118\t// queue\u2019s virtual start time is decremented by G - S.\n   119\tpackage queueset\n   120\t\n"

"func (cfgCtlr *configController) startRequest(ctx context.Context, rd RequestDigest,\n        noteFn func(fs *flowcontrol.FlowSchema, pl *flowcontrol.PriorityLevelConfiguration, flowDistinguisher string),\n        workEstimator func() fcrequest.WorkEstimate,\n        queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn) (fs *flowcontrol.FlowSchema, pl *flowcontrol.PriorityLevelConfiguration, isExempt bool, req fq.Request, startWaitingTime time.Time) {\n        klog.V(7).Infof(\"startRequest(%#+v)\", rd)\n        cfgCtlr.lock.RLock()\n        defer cfgCtlr.lock.RUnlock()\n        var selectedFlowSchema, catchAllFlowSchema *flowcontrol.FlowSchema\n        for _, fs := range cfgCtlr.flowSchemas {\n                if matchesFlowSchema(rd, fs) {\n                        selectedFlowSchema = fs\n                        break\n                }\n                if fs.Name == flowcontrol.FlowSchemaNameCatchAll {\n                        catchAllFlowSchema = fs\n                }\n        }\n        if selectedFlowSchema == nil {\n                // This should never happen. "func hashFlowID(fsName, fDistinguisher string) uint64 {\n        hash := sha256.New()\n        var sep = [1]byte{0}\n        hash.Write([]byte(fsName))\n        hash.Write(sep[:])\n        hash.Write([]byte(fDistinguisher))\n        var sum [32]byte\n        hash.Sum(sum[:0])\n        return binary.LittleEndian.Uint64(sum[:8])\n}\n\nfunc relDiff(x, y float64) float64 {\n        diff := math.Abs(x - y)\n        den := math.Max(math.Abs(x), math.Abs(y))\n        if den == 0 {"

  "file_text": "# Kubernetes API Priority and Fairness: QueueSet Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [System Overview](#1-system-overview)\n2. [Core Abstractions and Data Structures](#2-core-abstractions-and-data-structures)\n3. [Virtual Time and the R(t) Progress Meter](#3-virtual-time-and-the-rt-progress-meter)\n4. [Work Estimation: Seats and SeatSeconds](#4-work-estimation-seats-and-seatseconds)\n5. [Shuffle Sharding: Queue Assignment](#5-shuffle-sharding-queue-assignment)\n6. [Request Lifecycle: From Arrival to Completion](#6-request-lifecycle-from-arrival-to-completion)\n7. [Dispatch Algorithm: findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked](#7-dispatch-algorithm-finddispatchqueuetoboundlocked)\n8. [Anti-Windup: boundNextDispatchLocked](#8-anti-windup-boundnextdispatchlocked)\n9. [Epoch Advancement: Overflow Prevention](#9-epoch-advancement-overflow-prevention)\n10. [Concurrency Borrowing and Dynamic Allocation](#10-concurrency-borrowing-and-dynamic-allocation)\n11. [Synchronization: The Promise/WriteOnce Primitive](#11-synchronization-the-promisewriteonce-primitive)\n12. [Metrics Instrumentation](#12-metrics-instrumentation)\n13. [Debug Endpoints](#13-debug-endpoints)\n14. [Fairness Tradeoffs and Design Analysis](#14-fairness-tradeoffs-and-design-analysis)\n15. [Configuration Reference](#15-configuration-reference)\n\n---\n\n## 1. System Overview\n\nAPI Priority and Fairness (APF) is the Kubernetes mechanism that prevents any single client or workload from monopolizing the kube-apiserver. It replaces the older `--max-requests-inflight` and `--max-mutating-requests-inflight` flags with a richer model that classifies requests into flows, assigns them to priority levels, and dispatches them using a fair-queuing algorithm adapted from network packet scheduling.\n\n### 1.1 The Two-Object Model\n\nAPF is configured through two Kubernetes API object types:\n\n**FlowSchema** (`flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1`) classifies incoming requests. Each FlowSchema specifies:\n- A set of matching rules (subjects, resource rules, non-resource rules).\n- A reference to a `PriorityLevelConfiguration`.\n- A `DistinguisherMethod` (`ByUser` or `ByNamespace`) that determines how requests within the same FlowSchema are separated into distinct flows.\n- A numeric `matchingPrecedence` \u2014 lower numbers win; the first matching FlowSchema wins.\n\n**PriorityLevelConfiguration** (`flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1`) defines the queuing and dispatching behavior for a class of requests. It specifies:\n- `nominalConcurrencyShares` \u2014 a relative weight used to compute the nominal concurrency limit.\n- `lendablePercent` \u2014 the fraction of the nominal limit that can be lent to other levels.\n- `borrowingLimitPercent` \u2014 the maximum fraction above nominal that this level can borrow.\n- Queuing parameters: number of queues, queue length limit, hand size.\n- `LimitResponse.Type`: either `Queue` (buffer and dispatch fairly) or `Reject` (drop immediately when over limit).\n\nTwo mandatory objects always exist and cannot be deleted:\n- `exempt` FlowSchema + PriorityLevelConfiguration: system-critical requests (e.g., from `system:masters`) bypass all limiting.\n- `catch-all` FlowSchema + PriorityLevelConfiguration: a safety net that matches any request not matched by any other FlowSchema.\n\n### 1.2 The configController\n\nThe `configController` (`apf_controller.go`) is the central coordinator. It:\n1. Watches FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects via informers.\n2. Recomputes the sorted FlowSchema list and the per-priority-level `QueueSet` instances whenever configuration changes.\n3. Runs a periodic borrowing adjustment loop (`updateBorrowing`) every 10 seconds.\n4. Exposes the `Handle()` method that the HTTP handler chain calls for every non-exempt request.\n\n### 1.3 Request Classification Path\n\n```\nHTTP Request\n    \u2502\n    \u25bc\nconfigController.Handle()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500\u25ba startRequest()\n    \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u25ba Iterate flowSchemas (sorted by matchingPrecedence)\n    \u2502       \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u25ba matchesFlowSchema() \u2192 first match wins\n    \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u25ba computeFlowDistinguisher()  (ByUser or ByNamespace)\n    \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u25ba hashFlowID(fsName, flowDistinguisher)  \u2192 uint64 hash\n    \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u25ba workEstimator()  \u2192 WorkEstimate{InitialSeats, FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency}\n    \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u25ba plState.queues.StartRequest(...)  \u2192 fq.Request\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500\u25ba req.Finish(execFn)\n            \u2502\n            \u251c\u2500\u25ba [if queued] wait for decision (execute or cancel)\n            \u2514\u2500\u25ba [if execute] run execFn(), then finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n```\n\nThe flow distinguisher is hashed together with the FlowSchema name using SHA-256 (truncated to 64 bits) to produce a stable, uniformly distributed `hashValue` that drives shuffle sharding.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Core Abstractions and Data Structures\n\n### 2.1 queueSet\n\n`queueSet` (`queueset/queueset.go`) is the central struct implementing the `QueueSet` interface for one non-exempt priority level. Fields are divided into two groups by a `sync.Mutex`:\n\n**Immutable after construction:**\n```\nclock                    eventclock.Interface   // real or fake clock\nestimatedServiceDuration time.Duration          // G = 3ms, the service-time guess\nreqsGaugePair            metrics.RatioedGaugePair\nexecSeatsGauge           metrics.RatioedGauge\nseatDemandIntegrator     metrics.Gauge\npromiseFactory           promiseFactory\n```\n\n**Mutable (lock required):**\n```\nqCfg              fq.QueuingConfig       // DesiredNumQueues, QueueLengthLimit, HandSize\ndCfg              fq.DispatchingConfig   // ConcurrencyLimit, ConcurrencyDenominator\ndealer            *shufflesharding.Dealer\nqueues            []*queue               // may be longer than DesiredNumQueues during drain\ncurrentR          fqrequest.SeatSeconds  // global virtual time progress meter\nlastRealTime      time.Time\nrobinIndex        int                    // last queue index visited in round-robin\ntotRequestsWaiting    int\ntotRequestsExecuting  int\nrequestsExecutingSet  sets.Set[*request] // used only when DesiredNumQueues == 0\ntotSeatsInUse     int\ntotSeatsWaiting   int\nenqueues          int                    // total enqueue count, used for round-robin offset\n```\n\n### 2.2 queue\n\nEach `queue` represents one virtual flow bucket:\n\n```go\ntype queue struct {\n    requestsWaiting   fifo                  // FIFO list of waiting requests\n    nextDispatchR     fqrequest.SeatSeconds // virtual start time of next dispatch\n    requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]    // currently executing requests\n    index             int                   // position in queueSet.queues\n    seatsInUse        int                   // seats occupied by executing requests\n}\n```\n\n`nextDispatchR` is the key state variable. It tracks the queue's virtual start time \u2014 the R value at which the next request from this queue will be dispatched in the virtual world. This is the implementation of the \"virtual start time\" concept from the original fair queuing paper, adapted to avoid storing per-request virtual finish times explicitly.\n\n### 2.3 request\n\n```go\ntype request struct {\n    ctx               context.Context\n    qs                *queueSet\n    flowDistinguisher string\n    fsName            string\n    queue             *queue              // nil if no queuing (DesiredNumQueues < 1)\n    workEstimate      completedWorkEstimate\n    decision          promise.WriteOnce   // set to decisionExecute or decisionCancel\n    arrivalTime       time.Time\n    arrivalR          fqrequest.SeatSeconds  // R(arrivalTime), for anti-windup\n    startTime         time.Time\n    removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc\n    waitStarted       bool\n}\n```\n\nThe `decision` field is a `WriteOnce` promise. It is set exactly once \u2014 either to `decisionExecute` (by the dispatcher) or to `decisionCancel` (by context cancellation). The goroutine serving the request blocks on `decision.Get()` until one of these outcomes is determined.\n\n### 2.4 completedWorkEstimate\n\n```go\ntype completedWorkEstimate struct {\n    fcrequest.WorkEstimate          // InitialSeats, FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency\n    totalWork fcrequest.SeatSeconds // InitialSeats*G + FinalSeats*AdditionalLatency\n    finalWork fcrequest.SeatSeconds // FinalSeats*AdditionalLatency\n}\n```\n\n`totalWork` is the quantity added to `queue.nextDispatchR` when a request is dispatched. It represents the total virtual cost of the request: the initial phase cost (using the estimated service duration `G`) plus the final phase cost (using the actual `AdditionalLatency`).\n\n### 2.5 fifo / requestFIFO\n\nThe waiting list within each queue is a doubly-linked list (`container/list`) wrapped in a `requestFIFO` struct that maintains a running `queueSum`:\n\n```go\ntype queueSum struct {\n    InitialSeatsSum int\n    MaxSeatsSum     int\n    TotalWorkSum    fqrequest.SeatSeconds\n}\n```\n\n`Enqueue()` returns a `removeFromFIFOFunc` closure that removes the specific list element in O(1) time. This is used for context-cancellation removal without scanning the list. The `queueSum` is updated incrementally on every enqueue and dequeue, making O(1) access to aggregate queue statistics that are needed by both the shuffle-sharding selection and the virtual-time rate calculation.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Virtual Time and the R(t) Progress Meter\n\n### 3.1 Theoretical Foundation\n\nAPF adapts the Weighted Fair Queuing (WFQ) algorithm from Demers, Keshav, and Shenker (1989). In the original network model, a router maintains a virtual clock R(t) that advances at a rate inversely proportional to the number of active flows, ensuring each flow gets an equal share of bandwidth over time.\n\nFor the apiserver, the adaptation makes three key changes:\n\n**Change 1: Multiple concurrent requests.** Instead of one packet at a time, the apiserver can execute `C` requests simultaneously (where `C` is the concurrency limit). The virtual clock rate is scaled by `C`.\n\n**Change 2: Variable-width requests.** Requests occupy a variable number of \"seats\" (1 to N). The virtual cost of a request is `seats \u00d7 duration` rather than just `packet_size`.\n\n**Change 3: Unknown service time.** Unlike network packets whose size is known before transmission, request execution duration is unknown until completion. APF uses a fixed estimate `G = 3ms` for dispatch decisions and corrects `nextDispatchR` retroactively when the actual duration is known.\n\n### 3.2 The Virtual Time Rate Formula\n\nAt any real time `t`, the rate of virtual time advancement is:\n\n```\ndR/dt = min(C, \u03a3_q reqs(q,t)) / NEQ(t)\n```\n\nWhere:\n- `C` = `dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit` \u2014 the concurrency limit\n- `\u03a3_q reqs(q,t)` = total seats currently in use across all queues\n- `NEQ(t)` = number of non-empty queues (queues with waiting or executing requests)\n\nThis formula has two important properties:\n1. When all `C` seats are occupied, virtual time advances at rate `C / NEQ(t)`, giving each active queue `1/NEQ(t)` of the total capacity per unit time.\n2. When fewer than `C` seats are occupied (the system is underloaded), virtual time advances more slowly, proportional to actual utilization. This prevents queues from accumulating virtual credit during idle periods.\n\n### 3.3 Implementation: syncTimeLocked and getVirtualTimeRatioLocked\n\n```go\n// syncTimeLocked \u2014 called on every lock acquisition\nfunc (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n    realNow := qs.clock.Now()\n    timeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n    qs.lastRealTime = realNow\n    incrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n    qs.currentR += incrR\n    // ... overflow check and epoch advancement\n}\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() float64 {\n    activeQueues := 0\n    seatsRequested := 0\n    for _, queue := range qs.queues {\n        seatsRequested += queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum\n        if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {\n            activeQueues++\n        }\n    }\n    if activeQueues == 0 {\n        return 0\n    }\n    return math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n}\n```\n\n**Critical detail:** `seatsRequested` uses `MaxSeatsSum` (the maximum of `InitialSeats` and `FinalSeats` for each waiting request) rather than `InitialSeatsSum`. This is because the virtual time rate must reflect the maximum potential demand of each queue, not just its current phase demand. Using `MaxSeats` ensures that wide requests (e.g., those with large `FinalSeats` for watch event fanout) are properly accounted for in the rate calculation.\n\n**Lazy evaluation:** Virtual time is not updated on a timer. It is updated lazily \u2014 only when the lock is acquired \u2014 via `lockAndSyncTime()`. This means `currentR` always reflects the state as of the last lock acquisition, not the current wall-clock time. This is correct because all state modifications happen under the lock, so the virtual time only needs to be current at the moment of each state change.\n\n### 3.4 The nextDispatchR State Variable\n\nRather than storing per-request virtual finish times, APF uses a single `nextDispatchR` per queue. This is the queue's \"virtual start time\" \u2014 the R value at which the next request from this queue will begin service in the virtual world.\n\n**When a queue becomes non-empty from empty:**\n```go\nqueue.nextDispatchR = qs.currentR  // start from current virtual time\n```\n\n**When a request is dispatched (dequeued for execution):**\n```go\nqueue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n// totalWork = InitialSeats*G + FinalSeats*AdditionalLatency\n```\n\n**When a request finishes with actual service duration S:**\n```go\nqueue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(float64(r.InitialSeats()), G - S)\n// Correction: if S < G, nextDispatchR was advanced too far; pull it back.\n// If S > G, nextDispatchR was not advanced far enough; push it forward.\n```\n\nThis retroactive correction is the key mechanism for handling unknown service times. The virtual finish time of request J in a queue (counting from J=1 at the head) is:\n\n```\nVirtualFinish(J) = nextDispatchR + J * totalWork(J)\n```\n\nThe dispatch algorithm selects the queue whose head request has the minimum virtual finish time, which is:\n\n```\ncurrentVirtualFinish = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n```\n\n### 3.5 SeatSeconds: The Unit of Virtual Work\n\n`SeatSeconds` is a fixed-point `uint64` type with a scale factor of `1e8`:\n\n```go\ntype SeatSeconds uint64\nconst ssScale = 1e8\n// SeatSeconds(n) represents n/1e8 seat-seconds\n```\n\nThe conversion from seats and duration:\n```go\nfunc SeatsTimesDuration(seats float64, duration time.Duration) SeatSeconds {\n    return SeatSeconds(int64(math.Round(\n        seats * float64(duration/time.Nanosecond) / (1e9 / ssScale)\n    )))\n}\n```\n\nThis gives a resolution of `1e8 / 1e9 = 0.1` nanosecond-seats, which is more than sufficient for practical request durations. The maximum representable value is `math.MaxUint64 / 1e8 \u2248 1.84 \u00d7 10^11` seat-seconds \u2014 approximately 5,840 years of single-seat work, which is why epoch advancement (Section 9) is needed to prevent overflow in long-running servers.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Work Estimation: Seats and SeatSeconds\n\n### 4.1 WorkEstimate Structure\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimate struct {\n    InitialSeats      uint64        // seats occupied during main execution\n    FinalSeats        uint64        // seats occupied during AdditionalLatency phase\n    AdditionalLatency time.Duration // duration of the final phase after execFn() returns\n}\n```\n\nA request has two phases:\n1. **Initial phase**: `execFn()` runs, occupying `InitialSeats` seats. Duration is unknown until completion.\n2. **Final phase**: After `execFn()` returns, `FinalSeats` seats are held for `AdditionalLatency`. This models the cost of downstream work triggered by the request (e.g., watch event fanout).\n\n`MaxSeats()` returns `max(InitialSeats, FinalSeats)`. This is used for:\n- Checking whether a request can be accommodated (`canAccommodateSeatsLocked`).\n- Computing `totSeatsWaiting` and `totSeatsInUse`.\n- The anti-windup bound (`boundNextDispatchLocked`).\n\n### 4.2 List Request Estimator\n\nList requests are the most expensive in terms of memory and CPU because they must serialize potentially large collections of objects. The estimator (`request/list_work_estimator.go`) uses:\n\n```\nseats = clamp(ceil(estimatedObjectCount * objectSize / bytesPerSeat), minSeats, maxSeats)\n```\n\nWhere:\n- `bytesPerSeat = 100,000` bytes (100 KB per seat)\n- `maxObjectSize = 1,500,000` bytes (1.5 MB, the etcd recommended client request size)\n- `minSeats` = configured minimum (default 1)\n- `maxSeats` = `min(maxSeatsFn(priorityLevel), MaximumListSeatsLimit)`\n\nThe object count is estimated from:\n1. If `metadata.name` is specified in the field selector \u2192 treat as a single-object get \u2192 1 seat.\n2. If `limit` is specified \u2192 use `min(limit, totalObjectCount)`.\n3. If `resourceVersion=0` (serve from cache) and streaming is enabled \u2192 use `cacheWithStreamingMaxMemoryUsage / bytesPerSeat`.\n4. Otherwise \u2192 use the total object count from the storage stats tracker.\n\nFor `watch` requests with `SendInitialEvents`, the list estimator is used because the initial event burst has the same cost profile as a list.\n\n### 4.3 Mutating Request Estimator\n\nMutating requests (create, update, patch, delete) trigger watch event notifications to all interested watchers. The estimator (`request/mutating_work_estimator.go`) models this fanout cost:\n\n```\nfinalSeats = ceil(watchCount / WatchesPerSeat)\nfinalWork  = finalSeats * eventAdditionalDuration\n```\n\nThe `finalWork` is then reshaped to fit within the concurrency limit:\n```go\nif finalSeats > uint64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit) {\n    finalSeats = uint64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)\n    additionalLatency = finalWork.DurationPerSeat(float64(finalSeats))\n}\n```\n\nThis reshaping preserves the total work (`finalSeats \u00d7 additionalLatency = constant`) while ensuring `FinalSeats` never exceeds the concurrency limit, which would make the request permanently undispatchable.\n\nThe `AdditionalLatency` is transparent to the caller: `execFn()` returns before the final phase begins. The final phase is implemented via `clock.EventAfterDuration()`, which fires a goroutine after `AdditionalLatency` elapses to release the final seats and trigger another dispatch round.\n\n### 4.4 Default Estimator\n\nAll other verbs (get, watch without SendInitialEvents, proxy, etc.) receive:\n```\nWorkEstimate{InitialSeats: minimumSeats}  // typically 1\n```\n\n### 4.5 Max Seats Constraint\n\nThe maximum seats for any request at a given priority level is:\n```\nmaxSeats = max(1, min(0.15 * nominalCL, nominalCL / handSize))\n```\n\nThis ensures:\n- No single request can monopolize more than 15% of the priority level's nominal capacity.\n- Wide requests cannot exceed what shuffle sharding can accommodate (a request wider than `nominalCL / handSize` would starve queues that don't have enough seats available).\n\n---\n\n## 5. Shuffle Sharding: Queue Assignment\n\n### 5.1 The Problem Shuffle Sharding Solves\n\nWith `N` queues and a simple hash-mod assignment, a misbehaving flow that fills its queue to capacity blocks only `1/N` of the total queue capacity. But if two flows happen to hash to the same queue, they interfere with each other. Shuffle sharding provides isolation: a flow's requests are spread across a small \"hand\" of queues, and the queue with the minimum backlog is chosen. This means a misbehaving flow can only affect the `handSize` queues in its hand, not all `N` queues.\n\nThe probability that two flows share at least one queue in their hands (and thus can interfere) is:\n\n```\nP(collision) \u2248 1 - (N-handSize)! * N! / ((N-2*handSize)! * N!^2)\n             \u2248 C(handSize, 1)^2 / N  for large N\n```\n\nFor `N=128, handSize=6`: `P(collision) \u2248 36/128 \u2248 28%`. For `N=128, handSize=8`: `P(collision) \u2248 64/128 = 50%`. The default of `handSize=8` with `N=64` queues gives good isolation while keeping the selection overhead bounded.\n\n### 5.2 The Dealer Algorithm\n\nThe `Dealer` (`pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`) implements a Fisher-Yates partial shuffle using the hash value as entropy:\n\n```go\nfunc (d *Dealer) Deal(hashValue uint64, pick func(int)) {\n    var remainders [15]int\n    // Phase 1: extract remainders from hash\n    for i := 0; i < d.handSize; i++ {\n        hashValueNext := hashValue / uint64(d.deckSize-i)\n        remainders[i] = int(hashValue - uint64(d.deckSize-i)*hashValueNext)\n        hashValue = hashValueNext\n    }\n    // Phase 2: reconstruct card indices using the Lehmer code\n    for i := 0; i < d.handSize; i++ {\n        card := remainders[i]\n        for j := i; j > 0; j-- {\n            if card >= remainders[j-1] {\n                card++\n            }\n        }\n        pick(card)\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis is a bijection from `[0, deckSize! / (deckSize-handSize)!)` to ordered hands of `handSize` distinct cards from a deck of `deckSize`. The required entropy is `ceil(log2(deckSize) * handSize)` bits, which must not exceed 60 bits (to avoid bias in the last card).\n\n### 5.3 Queue Selection Within the Hand\n\nAfter dealing the hand, `shuffleShardLocked` selects the queue with the minimum `TotalWorkSum`:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardLocked(hashValue uint64, ...) int {\n    var backHand [8]int\n    hand := qs.dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\n    handSize := len(hand)\n    offset := qs.enqueues % handSize  // round-robin starting point within hand\n    qs.enqueues++\n    bestQueueIdx := -1\n    minQueueSeatSeconds := fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds\n    for i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n        queueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n        queue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n        thisQueueSeatSeconds := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().TotalWorkSum\n        if thisQueueSeatSeconds < minQueueSeatSeconds {\n            minQueueSeatSeconds = thisQueueSeatSeconds\n            bestQueueIdx = queueIdx\n        }\n    }\n    return bestQueueIdx\n}\n```\n\n**The `offset` trick:** The starting position within the hand rotates with each enqueue (`offset = enqueues % handSize`). This breaks ties between equally-loaded queues in a round-robin fashion, preventing systematic bias toward the first card in the hand when multiple queues have the same `TotalWorkSum`.\n\n**Why `TotalWorkSum` not queue length?** Using total work (seat-seconds) rather than request count correctly handles variable-width requests. A queue with 3 single-seat requests has less backlog than a queue with 1 ten-seat request, even though the latter has fewer requests.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Request Lifecycle: From Arrival to Completion\n\n### 6.1 Phase 0: No-Queue Mode (DesiredNumQueues < 1)\n\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues == 0`, the QueueSet acts as a pure concurrency limiter with no queuing:\n\n```go\nif qs.qCfg.DesiredNumQueues < 1 {\n    if !qs.canAccommodateSeatsLocked(workEstimate.MaxSeats()) {\n        // Reject immediately\n        metrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"concurrency-limit\")\n        return nil, qs.isIdleLocked()\n    }\n    req = qs.dispatchSansQueueLocked(...)\n    return req, false\n}\n```\n\n`canAccommodateSeatsLocked` checks:\n- `DesiredNumQueues < 0`: always true (exempt mode).\n- `seats > ConcurrencyLimit`: true only if `totRequestsExecuting == 0` (allow one oversized request to proceed when the system is otherwise idle).\n- `totSeatsInUse + seats > ConcurrencyLimit`: false (not enough room).\n\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues < 0`, the QueueSet is in \"exempt\" mode: all requests are dispatched immediately regardless of concurrency.\n\n### 6.2 Phase 1: Shuffle Sharding and Enqueue\n\n```\nStartRequest()\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500\u25ba lockAndSyncTime()          // acquire lock, advance virtual time\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500\u25ba shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()\n    \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u25ba shuffleShardLocked()     // pick queue via shuffle sharding\n    \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u25ba construct request{}      // set arrivalR = currentR\n    \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u25ba rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked()\n    \u2502       \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u2502       \u251c\u2500\u25ba if totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND\n    \u2502       \u2502       \u2502      queue.Length() >= QueueLengthLimit \u2192 return false (reject)\n    \u2502       \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u25ba enqueueToBoundLocked()\n    \u2502       \u2502               \u2502\n    \u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u25ba if queue was empty: nextDispatchR = currentR\n    \u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u25ba queue.requestsWaiting.Enqueue(req)\n    \u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u25ba totRequestsWaiting++, totSeatsWaiting += MaxSeats\n    \u2502       \u2502               \u2514\u2500\u25ba boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)  // anti-windup\n    \u2502       \u2502\n    \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u25ba return req (or nil if rejected)\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500\u25ba dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()  // try to dispatch immediately\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500\u25ba return req, false\n```\n\n**Rejection condition:** A request is rejected (with reason `\"queue-full\"`) only when *both* conditions hold simultaneously:\n- The concurrency limit is fully occupied (`totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit`).\n- The selected queue is at its length limit (`queue.Length() >= QueueLengthLimit`).\n\nIf either condition is false, the request is enqueued. This means a request can be enqueued even when the concurrency limit is full (it will wait), and it can be dispatched immediately even when the queue is at its length limit (if there is concurrency available).\n\n### 6.3 Phase 2: Dispatch Loop\n\nAfter enqueuing, `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()` runs a greedy dispatch loop:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() {\n    for qs.totRequestsWaiting != 0 &&\n        qs.totSeatsInUse < qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n        qs.dispatchLocked() {\n    }\n}\n```\n\nEach call to `dispatchLocked()` selects one request via `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()` (Section 7) and dispatches it by:\n1. Removing it from its queue's FIFO list.\n2. Setting `request.decision` to `decisionExecute` via the promise.\n3. Moving it to `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n4. Incrementing `totSeatsInUse` and `queue.seatsInUse` by `MaxSeats()`.\n5. Advancing `queue.nextDispatchR` by `request.totalWork()`.\n\n### 6.4 Phase 3: Waiting for a Decision\n\nThe goroutine serving the request calls `req.Finish(execFn)`, which internally calls `req.wait()`:\n\n```go\nfunc (req *request) wait() (bool, bool) {\n    decisionAny := req.decision.Get()  // BLOCKS until Set() is called\n    qs.lockAndSyncTime(req.ctx)\n    defer qs.lock.Unlock()\n    // ...\n    switch decisionAny {\n    case decisionCancel:\n        // Context was cancelled while waiting; remove from queue\n        if req.removeFromQueueLocked() != nil {\n            qs.totRequestsWaiting--\n            qs.totSeatsWaiting -= req.MaxSeats()\n            metrics.AddReject(req.ctx, ..., \"time-out\")\n        }\n        return false, qs.isIdleLocked()\n    case decisionExecute:\n        return true, false\n    }\n}\n```\n\n`decision.Get()` blocks on a channel select between `setCh` (closed when `Set()` is called) and `doneCtx.Done()` (the request's context). If the context is cancelled before dispatch, `Set(decisionCancel)` is effectively called, and the request is removed from the queue.\n\n### 6.5 Phase 4: Execution and Completion\n\nIf `wait()` returns `(true, false)`, `execFn()` is called. After it returns:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) finishRequestLocked(r *request) {\n    qs.totRequestsExecuting--\n    actualServiceDuration := now.Sub(r.startTime)\n\n    if r.workEstimate.AdditionalLatency <= 0 {\n        // No final phase: release seats immediately\n        releaseSeatsLocked()\n    } else {\n        // Final phase: hold FinalSeats for AdditionalLatency\n        qs.clock.EventAfterDuration(func(_ time.Time) {\n            qs.lockAndSyncTime(r.ctx)\n            defer qs.lock.Unlock()\n            releaseSeatsLocked()\n            qs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n        }, r.workEstimate.AdditionalLatency)\n    }\n\n    if r.queue != nil {\n        r.queue.requestsExecuting.Delete(r)\n        // Retroactive correction of nextDispatchR\n        r.queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(\n            float64(r.InitialSeats()),\n            qs.estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration,\n        )\n        qs.boundNextDispatchLocked(r.queue)\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe retroactive correction adjusts `nextDispatchR` based on the difference between the estimated service duration `G` and the actual duration `S`:\n- If `S < G` (request finished faster than estimated): `nextDispatchR` was advanced too far; it is decremented by `InitialSeats * (G - S)`.\n- If `S > G` (request ran longer than estimated): `nextDispatchR` was not advanced far enough; it is incremented by `InitialSeats * (S - G)`.\n\nAfter correction, `boundNextDispatchLocked` is called to apply the anti-windup constraint (Section 8).\n\n### 6.6 Queue Lifecycle\n\nQueues are created eagerly when `DesiredNumQueues` increases, but removed lazily:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) removeQueueIfEmptyLocked(r *request) {\n    if len(qs.queues) > qs.qCfg.DesiredNumQueues &&\n        r.queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 &&\n        r.queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n        qs.queues = removeQueueAndUpdateIndexes(qs.queues, r.queue.index)\n        if qs.robinIndex >= r.queue.index {\n            qs.robinIndex--\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWhen `DesiredNumQueues` is reduced (e.g., during a configuration change), excess queues are not immediately destroyed. They continue to drain naturally, and are removed only when they become empty. This ensures in-flight requests are not disrupted by configuration changes.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Dispatch Algorithm: findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked\n\nThis is the heart of the fair queuing implementation. It selects which queue to dispatch from next.\n\n### 7.1 The Algorithm\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked() (*queue, *request) {\n    minVirtualFinish := fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds\n    var minQueue *queue\n    var minIndex int\n    nq := len(qs.queues)\n\n    for range qs.queues {\n        qs.robinIndex = (qs.robinIndex + 1) % nq\n        queue := qs.queues[qs.robinIndex]\n        oldestWaiting, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n        if oldestWaiting != nil {\n            currentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\n            if currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n                minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n                minQueue = queue\n                minIndex = qs.robinIndex\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    oldestReqFromMinQueue, _ := minQueue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if !qs.canAccommodateSeatsLocked(oldestReqFromMinQueue.MaxSeats()) {\n        return nil, nil  // cannot dispatch; not enough seats\n    }\n    oldestReqFromMinQueue.removeFromQueueLocked()\n\n    // Clamp FinalSeats to ConcurrencyLimit if needed\n    if oldestReqFromMinQueue.workEstimate.FinalSeats > uint64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit) {\n        finalSeats := uint64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)\n        additionalLatency := oldestReqFromMinQueue.workEstimate.finalWork.DurationPerSeat(float64(finalSeats))\n        oldestReqFromMinQueue.workEstimate.FinalSeats = finalSeats\n        oldestReqFromMinQueue.workEstimate.AdditionalLatency = additionalLatency\n    }\n\n    qs.robinIndex = minIndex  // next round starts after the chosen queue\n    return minQueue, oldestReqFromMinQueue\n}\n```\n\n### 7.2 Virtual Finish Time Selection\n\nThe dispatch criterion is: **select the queue whose head request has the minimum virtual finish time**.\n\n```\nvirtualFinish(queue) = queue.nextDispatchR + head(queue).totalWork()\n```\n\nThis is equivalent to selecting the queue that has done the least virtual work so far, adjusted for the cost of its next request. A queue that has been idle (or whose requests finished faster than estimated) will have a lower `nextDispatchR` and thus a lower virtual finish time, giving it priority in the next dispatch round.\n\n### 7.3 Round-Robin Tie Breaking\n\nThe outer loop iterates all queues in round-robin order (starting from `robinIndex + 1`). The minimum virtual finish time is tracked globally. When the loop ends, `robinIndex` is set to `minIndex` \u2014 the index of the chosen queue. This means the next dispatch round starts from the queue *after* the one just dispatched, giving other queues with equal virtual finish times a chance to be selected first.\n\nThis tie-breaking is important for fairness when multiple queues have the same `nextDispatchR` (e.g., when they all started from the same virtual time). Without it, the same queue would always win ties, creating systematic unfairness.\n\n### 7.4 Seat Availability Check\n\nAfter selecting the minimum-virtual-finish queue, the algorithm checks whether the head request can actually be dispatched:\n\n```go\nif !qs.canAccommodateSeatsLocked(oldestReqFromMinQueue.MaxSeats()) {\n    return nil, nil\n}\n```\n\nIf the head request requires more seats than are currently available, dispatch stops entirely \u2014 even if other queues have requests that would fit. This is a deliberate design choice: dispatching a smaller request from a different queue would violate the fairness ordering (the minimum-virtual-finish queue should go next). The system waits until enough seats are freed.\n\n**Implication:** A single wide request at the head of the minimum-virtual-finish queue can block all dispatch. This is the primary source of head-of-line blocking in APF. The `AddDispatchWithNoAccommodation` metric tracks this condition.\n\n### 7.5 FinalSeats Clamping\n\nIf a request's `FinalSeats` exceeds the concurrency limit (which can happen if the watch count estimator produces a very large value), the seats are clamped to `ConcurrencyLimit` and `AdditionalLatency` is extended proportionally to preserve total work:\n\n```\nnewAdditionalLatency = finalWork / newFinalSeats\n                     = (oldFinalSeats * oldAdditionalLatency) / ConcurrencyLimit\n```\n\nThis ensures the request can eventually be dispatched (its final phase will fit within the concurrency limit) while preserving the total accounting of work done.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Anti-Windup: boundNextDispatchLocked\n\n### 8.1 The Windup Problem\n\nIn standard fair queuing, all non-empty queues are allocated the same virtual time rate. But in APF, a queue that cannot use its full allocation (because its requests are narrow or infrequent) does not go empty \u2014 it accumulates a progressively earlier `nextDispatchR` relative to busier queues. When this queue eventually receives a burst of requests, it has a very low `nextDispatchR` and will be dispatched preferentially for a long time, potentially starving other queues. This is the \"windup\" problem.\n\n### 8.2 The Fix\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) boundNextDispatchLocked(queue *queue) {\n    oldestReqFromMinQueue, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldestReqFromMinQueue == nil {\n        return\n    }\n    var virtualStartBound = oldestReqFromMinQueue.arrivalR\n    if queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound {\n        queue.nextDispatchR = virtualStartBound\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe constraint is: **`nextDispatchR` must not be less than the arrival virtual time of the oldest waiting request**.\n\n`arrivalR` is set to `qs.currentR` at the moment the request arrives. This means a queue's virtual start time can never be earlier than when its oldest waiting request arrived. A queue that was idle cannot \"save up\" virtual time credit from before its current requests arrived.\n\n**When is it called?**\n- After every enqueue (`enqueueToBoundLocked` calls `boundNextDispatchLocked` via `rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked`).\n- After every dispatch (`dispatchLocked` calls it via `defer`).\n- After every finish (`finishRequestLocked` calls it after the retroactive correction).\n- After context cancellation removes a request from the queue.\n\nThe suffix `ToBound` in method names (`rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked`, `enqueueToBoundLocked`) signals that the caller must follow up with `boundNextDispatchLocked`. This naming convention is documented in the `queueSet` struct comment.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Epoch Advancement: Overflow Prevention\n\n### 9.1 The Problem\n\n`currentR` is a monotonically increasing `uint64` (as `SeatSeconds`). In a long-running apiserver with sustained load, it will eventually overflow. The maximum value is `math.MaxUint64 / 1e8 \u2248 1.84 \u00d7 10^11` seat-seconds. At a rate of 1 seat-second per second (one request executing continuously), this would take ~5,840 years. But with `C = 3000` seats and `NEQ = 1` queue, the rate is 3000 seat-seconds per second, reducing the overflow time to ~1.9 years. With more queues and higher concurrency, overflow could occur sooner.\n\n### 9.2 The Solution: Epoch Advancement\n\nWhen `currentR` exceeds `highR = 3/4 * MaxSeatSeconds`, the epoch is advanced by subtracting `rDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds / 2` from all R values:\n\n```go\nconst rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\nconst highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2  // = 3/4 * MaxSeatSeconds\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n    qs.currentR -= rDecrement\n    for qIdx, queue := range qs.queues {\n        if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n            queue.nextDispatchR = 0  // safe to reset; will be overwritten on next arrival\n            continue\n        }\n        queue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n        queue.requestsWaiting.Walk(func(req *request) bool {\n            req.arrivalR -= rDecrement\n            return true\n        })\n    }\n    metrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)\n}\n```\n\n**Why subtract from `arrivalR` too?** The anti-windup bound uses `arrivalR` as a lower bound for `nextDispatchR`. If `arrivalR` were not decremented, the bound would be violated after epoch advancement (since `nextDispatchR` was decremented but `arrivalR` was not), potentially causing `boundNextDispatchLocked` to advance `nextDispatchR` back up, undoing the epoch advancement for that queue.\n\n**Empty queues:** For queues with no waiting or executing requests, `nextDispatchR` is reset to 0 rather than decremented. This is safe because the next arrival to an empty queue always sets `nextDispatchR = currentR`, overwriting whatever value was there. Resetting to 0 avoids potential underflow if `nextDispatchR` was already small.\n\n**The `highR` threshold:** Epoch advancement triggers at `3/4 * MaxSeatSeconds` and subtracts `1/2 * MaxSeatSeconds`, leaving `currentR` at `1/4 * MaxSeatSeconds`. This gives a comfortable margin before the next epoch advancement is needed.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Concurrency Borrowing and Dynamic Allocation\n\n### 10.1 The Three Concurrency Limits\n\nEach non-exempt priority level has three concurrency limits:\n\n```\nnominalCL = ceil(serverConcurrencyLimit * nominalConcurrencyShares / shareSum)\nminCL     = nominalCL - lendableCL\n           where lendableCL = round(nominalCL * lendablePercent / 100)\nmaxCL     = nominalCL + borrowingCL\n           where borrowingCL = round(nominalCL * borrowingLimitPercent / 100)\n                             = serverConcurrencyLimit  (if borrowingLimitPercent is nil)\n```\n\n- `nominalCL`: the baseline allocation, computed proportionally from `nominalConcurrencyShares`.\n- `minCL`: the minimum guaranteed allocation; the level will never be given less than this.\n- `maxCL`: the maximum allocation; the level will never be given more than this.\n\nThe `currentCL` (the actual concurrency limit used by the QueueSet) is dynamically adjusted between `minCL` and `maxCL` by the borrowing algorithm.\n\n### 10.2 Seat Demand Tracking\n\nEach priority level maintains a `seatDemandIntegrator` that tracks the time-weighted average of `totSeatsInUse + totSeatsWaiting`. This integrator is updated on every change to either quantity.\n\nEvery 10 seconds (`borrowingAdjustmentPeriod`), `updateBorrowing()` calls `Reset()` on each integrator to get the statistics for the last period:\n\n```go\ntype seatDemandStats struct {\n    avg          float64  // time-weighted average seat demand\n    stdDev       float64  // standard deviation\n    highWatermark float64 // maximum observed demand\n    smoothed     float64  // exponentially smoothed envelope\n}\n```\n\nThe smoothed value uses an exponential moving average of the \"envelope\" (max of avg and highWatermark):\n\n```go\nenvelope := math.Max(obs.Average, float64(obs.Max))\nstats.smoothed = math.Max(envelope,\n    seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient*stats.smoothed +\n    (1-seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient)*envelope)\n```\n\nWith `seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977`, the smoothing time constant is approximately `10s / (1 - 0.977) \u2248 435 seconds` (about 7 minutes). This means the smoothed demand responds slowly to decreases but quickly to increases (since `max(envelope, ...)` ensures the smoothed value never decreases faster than the exponential decay).\n\n### 10.3 The Borrowing Algorithm\n\n`updateBorrowingLocked()` runs the allocation algorithm:\n\n```go\nfunc (cfgCtlr *configController) updateBorrowingLocked(setCompleters bool, plStates map[string]*priorityLevelState) {\n    // Step 1: Compute minCurrentCL for each non-exempt level\n    for plName, plState := range plStates {\n        if plState.pl.Spec.Type == flowcontrol.PriorityLevelEnablementExempt {\n            // Exempt levels consume from the server limit but don't participate in borrowing\n            remainingServerCL -= cclOfExempt[plName]\n            continue\n        }\n        // minCurrentCL: the minimum of what this level needs right now\n        minCurrentCL = max(plState.minCL, min(plState.nominalCL, plState.seatDemandStats.highWatermark))\n        items = append(items, allocProblemItem{\n            target:     max(float64(minCurrentCL), plState.seatDemandStats.smoothed),\n            lowerBound: float64(plState.minCL),\n            upperBound: float64(plState.maxCL),\n        })\n    }\n\n    // Step 2: Solve the allocation problem\n    if remainingServerCL <= minCLSum {\n        // Not enough capacity even for minimums; give each level its minCL\n        shareFrac = float64(remainingServerCL - minCLSum) / float64(minCurrentCLSum - minCLSum)\n    } else {\n        allocs, fairFrac, err = computeConcurrencyAllocation(cfgCtlr.nominalCLSum, items)\n    }\n\n    // Step 3: Apply the computed currentCL to each QueueSet\n}\n```\n\n### 10.4 computeConcurrencyAllocation\n\nThis function solves a constrained proportional allocation problem:\n\n**Given:** A required total `requiredSum` and a list of classes, each with `target`, `lowerBound`, `upperBound`.\n\n**Find:** Allocations `allocs[J]` such that:\n1. `lowerBound[J] \u2264 allocs[J] \u2264 upperBound[J]` for all J.\n2. `\u03a3 allocs[J] = requiredSum`.\n3. There exists a `fairProp` such that for each J:\n   - `allocs[J] = fairProp * target[J]` (proportional allocation), OR\n   - `allocs[J] = lowerBound[J]` (lower-bound constrained), OR\n   - `allocs[J] = upperBound[J]` (upper-bound constrained).\n\nThe algorithm works by binary search on `fairProp`, finding the value that makes the sum of clamped allocations equal to `requiredSum`. Classes that hit their bounds are \"saturated\" and removed from the proportional allocation; the remaining capacity is redistributed among unsaturated classes.\n\n**Practical effect:** Priority levels with high demand (smoothed demand > nominalCL) borrow from levels with low demand (smoothed demand < nominalCL), up to their respective `maxCL` and `minCL` bounds. The total allocation always sums to `serverConcurrencyLimit`.\n\n---\n\n## 11. Synchronization: The Promise/WriteOnce Primitive\n\n### 11.1 Design\n\nThe `promise.WriteOnce` interface provides a one-shot, thread-safe value container:\n\n```go\ntype WriteOnce interface {\n    Set(value interface{}) bool  // returns true if this was the first Set\n    Get() interface{}            // blocks until Set is called or context is done\n}\n```\n\nThe implementation uses a channel for blocking and `sync.Once` for the write-once guarantee:\n\n```go\ntype promise struct {\n    doneCtx context.Context\n    doneVal interface{}\n    setCh   chan struct{}  // closed when Set() is called\n    onceler sync.Once\n    value   interface{}\n}\n\nfunc (p *promise) Get() interface{} {\n    select {\n    case <-p.setCh:\n    case <-p.doneCtx.Done():\n        p.Set(p.doneVal)\n    }\n    return p.value\n}\n\nfunc (p *promise) Set(value interface{}) bool {\n    var ans bool\n    p.onceler.Do(func() {\n        p.value = value\n        close(p.setCh)\n        ans = true\n    })\n    return ans\n}\n```\n\n### 11.2 Usage in APF\n\nEach `request` has one `decision` promise, created with:\n```go\ndecision: qs.promiseFactory(nil, ctx, decisionCancel)\n```\n\n- `initial = nil`: the promise starts unset (the request is not yet dispatched).\n- `doneCtx = ctx`: the request's context.\n- `doneVal = decisionCancel`: if the context is cancelled, the promise resolves to `decisionCancel`.\n\nThe dispatcher calls `decision.Set(decisionExecute)` under the lock. The serving goroutine calls `decision.Get()` without the lock (it blocks on the channel). This design ensures:\n\n1. **No lock contention during waiting:** The serving goroutine does not hold the lock while waiting for a dispatch decision. The lock is only acquired after `Get()` returns.\n2. **Exactly-once semantics:** `sync.Once` ensures that even if both the dispatcher and context cancellation race to set the decision, only one wins.\n3. **Context cancellation is free:** If the context is cancelled before dispatch, `Get()` returns immediately with `decisionCancel`. The serving goroutine then acquires the lock and removes the request from the queue.\n\n### 11.3 The Locking Protocol\n\nAPF uses a strict locking discipline:\n- `Set()` is always called with the queueSet lock held.\n- `Get()` is always called without the queueSet lock.\n\nThis prevents deadlock: the serving goroutine cannot hold the lock while blocking on `Get()`, and the dispatcher cannot block on `Get()` while holding the lock.\n\n---\n\n## 12. Metrics Instrumentation\n\nAPF exposes a rich set of Prometheus metrics under the `apiserver_flowcontrol_` namespace. All metrics are labeled by `priority_level` and/or `flow_schema`.\n\n### 12.1 Virtual Time Metrics (ALPHA)\n\n| Metric | Type | Description |\n|--------|------|-------------|\n| `current_r` | Gauge | `R(t)` \u2014 the current virtual time progress meter for each priority level. Useful for detecting stalls (R stops advancing when no requests are active). |\n| `dispatch_r` | Gauge | The `nextDispatchR` of the queue most recently dispatched from. |\n| `latest_s` | Gauge | The `nextDispatchR` of the queue selected for the last dispatch attempt. |\n| `next_s_bounds{bound=\"min\"}` | Gauge | Minimum `nextDispatchR` across all non-empty queues. |\n| `next_s_bounds{bound=\"max\"}` | Gauge | Maximum `nextDispatchR` across all non-empty queues. |\n| `next_discounted_s_bounds{bound=\"min/max\"}` | Gauge | Min/max of `nextDispatchR - estimatedWorkInProgress` across non-empty queues. The \"discounted\" value subtracts the estimated remaining work of currently executing requests, giving a better estimate of when each queue will next be ready to dispatch. |\n\nThe spread between `next_s_bounds{min}` and `next_s_bounds{max}` indicates fairness: a large spread means some queues are far ahead of others in virtual time, suggesting unfairness or a burst from one flow.\n\n### 12.2 Concurrency Metrics\n\n| Metric | Type | Stability | Description |\n|--------|------|-----------|-------------|\n| `current_inqueue_requests` | Gauge | BETA | Requests currently waiting in queues. |\n| `current_inqueue_seats` | Gauge | ALPHA | Seats demanded by waiting requests (sum of MaxSeats). |\n| `current_executing_requests` | Gauge | BETA | Requests currently in the initial execution phase. |\n| `current_executing_seats` | Gauge | BETA | Seats occupied by executing requests. |\n| `request_concurrency_in_use` | Gauge | ALPHA | Seats in use (same as executing seats but with different labeling). |\n| `request_concurrency_limit` | Gauge | ALPHA | The current concurrency limit (`currentCL`) for each priority level, broken down into `nominal`, `min`, and `max`. |\n\n### 12.3 Request Outcome Metrics\n\n| Metric | Type | Stability | Description |\n|--------|------|-----------|-------------|\n| `rejected_requests_total` | Counter | BETA | Requests rejected, labeled by `reason`: `concurrency-limit` (no-queue mode), `queue-full` (both concurrency and queue length limits hit), `time-out` (context cancelled while waiting). |\n| `dispatched_requests_total` | Counter | BETA | Requests successfully dispatched for execution. |\n\n### 12.4 Latency Metrics\n\n| Metric | Type | Stability | Description |\n|--------|------|-----------|-------------|\n| `request_wait_duration_seconds` | Histogram | BETA | Time spent waiting in queue, labeled by `execute` (true/false \u2014 whether the request was eventually executed). |\n| `request_execution_seconds` | Histogram | ALPHA | Time spent in the initial execution phase (duration of `execFn()`). |\n\n### 12.5 Seat Utilization Metrics\n\n| Metric | Type | Stability | Description |\n|--------|------|-----------|-------------|\n| `priority_level_seat_utilization` | TimingRatioHistogram | ALPHA | Fraction of seats in use at each nanosecond, for all execution phases. Buckets include 0.99 and 1.0 to reveal saturation. |\n| `priority_level_request_utilization` | TimingRatioHistogram | ALPHA | Fraction of the concurrency limit in use (waiting + executing), broken down by phase. |\n| `read_vs_write_current_requests` | TimingRatioHistogram | ALPHA | Fraction of limit in use, broken down by mutating vs. read-only. |\n\n### 12.6 Seat Demand and Borrowing Metrics\n\n| Metric | Type | Stability | Description |\n|--------|------|-----------|-------------|\n| `seat_fair_frac` | Gauge | ALPHA | The `fairProp` value from the last borrowing computation \u2014 the proportionality constant applied to each level's target demand. |\n| `priority_level_seat_count_samples` | TimingRatioHistogram | ALPHA | Observations of seat demand (executing + queued) as a fraction of `nominalCL`. |\n| `watch_count_samples` | Histogram | ALPHA | Distribution of watch counts observed by the mutating work estimator. |\n\n### 12.7 Epoch and Error Metrics\n\n| Metric | Type | Stability | Description |\n|--------|------|-----------|-------------|\n| `epoch_advance_total` | Counter | ALPHA | Number of epoch advancements, labeled by `success` (true/false). A `success=false` indicates an underflow during epoch advancement, which should never happen. |\n| `request_queue_length_after_enqueue` | Histogram | ALPHA | Queue length observed immediately after a request is enqueued. |\n| `work_estimated_seats` | Histogram | ALPHA | Distribution of seat estimates from the work estimator. |\n| `dispatch_with_no_accommodation_total` | Counter | ALPHA | Number of times the minimum-virtual-finish queue's head request could not be dispatched due to insufficient seats. High values indicate head-of-line blocking from wide requests. |\n\n---\n\n## 13. Debug Endpoints\n\nThe APF controller installs three debug endpoints (unlisted, not in the API discovery):\n\n### 13.1 `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_priority_levels`\n\nCSV output with one row per priority level:\n```\nPriorityLevelName, ActiveQueues, IsIdle, IsQuiescing, WaitingRequests, ExecutingRequests, DispatchedRequests, RejectedRequests, TimedoutRequests, CancelledRequests\n```\n\n### 13.2 `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_queues`\n\nCSV output with one row per queue per priority level:\n```\nPriorityLevelName, Index, PendingRequests, ExecutingRequests, SeatsInUse, NextDispatchR, InitialSeatsSum, MaxSeatsSum, TotalWorkSum\n```\n\n`NextDispatchR` is the queue's virtual start time in seat-seconds. Comparing `NextDispatchR` values across queues reveals fairness: queues with very different values indicate that some flows have consumed significantly more or less virtual time than others.\n\n### 13.3 `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_requests`\n\nCSV output with one row per request (waiting and executing), with optional `?includeRequestDetails=1` for user/resource information:\n```\nPriorityLevelName, FlowSchemaName, QueueIndex, RequestIndex, FlowDistinguisher, ArriveTime, InitialSeats, FinalSeats, AdditionalLatency, StartTime\n```\n\n---\n\n## 14. Fairness Tradeoffs and Design Analysis\n\n### 14.1 Fairness Guarantee: Bounded Divergence\n\nThe core fairness guarantee of APF (inherited from WFQ) is bounded divergence from ideal fair sharing. In ideal fair sharing, each of `N` active flows receives exactly `1/N` of the server's capacity. In APF, the actual allocation can diverge from ideal by at most `C` requests (where `C` is the concurrency limit), because up to `C` requests can be executing simultaneously, each potentially from a different flow.\n\nMore precisely: if flow A has received `W_A` seat-seconds of service and flow B has received `W_B` seat-seconds, and both have been continuously active, then:\n\n```\n|W_A - W_B| \u2264 C * G\n```\n\nWhere `G = 3ms` is the estimated service duration. This bound holds regardless of the number of flows, the distribution of request sizes, or the arrival pattern.\n\n### 14.2 The Unknown Service Time Problem\n\nThe most significant departure from classical WFQ is the unknown service time. APF handles this with the retroactive correction mechanism (Section 6.5), but this introduces a subtle fairness issue:\n\n**Scenario:** Flow A consistently submits requests that take 1ms (much less than `G = 3ms`). Flow B consistently submits requests that take 10ms (much more than `G`).\n\n- When A's requests finish, `nextDispatchR` is decremented by `InitialSeats * (G - 1ms) = InitialSeats * 2ms`. A's queue gets a \"refund\" for the overestimated work.\n- When B's requests finish, `nextDispatchR` is incremented by `InitialSeats * (10ms - G) = InitialSeats * 7ms`. B's queue is \"charged\" for the underestimated work.\n\nOver time, A's `nextDispatchR` will be lower than B's, giving A higher dispatch priority. This is actually the *correct* behavior: A's requests are cheaper, so A should be able to submit more of them per unit time. The fairness guarantee is in terms of seat-seconds consumed, not request count.\n\n### 14.3 Head-of-Line Blocking\n\nThe dispatch algorithm stops when the minimum-virtual-finish queue's head request cannot be accommodated (insufficient seats). This creates head-of-line blocking: a wide request blocks all dispatch, even if other queues have narrow requests that would fit.\n\n**Why not dispatch from other queues?** Dispatching a narrower request from a different queue would violate the fairness ordering. The minimum-virtual-finish queue has \"earned\" the right to go next; dispatching another queue first would give that queue an unfair advantage.\n\n**Mitigation:** The `FinalSeats` clamping (Section 7.5) ensures that no request's final phase exceeds the concurrency limit. The `maxSeats` constraint (Section 4.5) limits how wide any single request can be. Together, these bound the duration of head-of-line blocking.\n\n**Observable impact:** The `dispatch_with_no_accommodation_total` metric counts these events. High values indicate that wide requests are frequently blocking dispatch, which may warrant reducing `MaximumListSeatsLimit` or `MaximumMutatingSeatsLimit`.\n\n### 14.4 Shuffle Sharding Isolation vs. Fairness\n\nShuffle sharding provides isolation between flows at the cost of some fairness. Two flows that share a queue in their hands will interfere with each other: if one flow fills the shared queue, the other flow's requests may be rejected even though other queues in its hand have capacity.\n\nThe queue selection criterion (minimum `TotalWorkSum`) partially mitigates this: a flow will avoid a shared queue if it has more backlog than other queues in the hand. But if all queues in the hand are equally loaded, the flow has no choice.\n\n**The isolation-fairness tradeoff:** Increasing `handSize` improves isolation (lower probability of collision) but increases the overhead of queue selection (O(handSize) comparisons per enqueue). Increasing `DesiredNumQueues` also improves isolation but increases memory usage and the overhead of the dispatch loop (O(DesiredNumQueues) comparisons per dispatch).\n\nThe default configuration (`DesiredNumQueues=64, handSize=8`) is chosen to provide strong isolation (probability of two flows sharing a queue \u2248 50%) with acceptable overhead.\n\n### 14.5 The Estimated Service Duration G\n\nThe choice of `G = 3ms` is a fixed constant in the code. It affects:\n\n1. **Dispatch ordering:** Requests with `totalWork` close to `G * InitialSeats` will have similar virtual finish times, making dispatch order nearly FIFO within a queue. Requests with very different `totalWork` values will be ordered by their virtual cost.\n\n2. **Retroactive correction magnitude:** If actual service times are consistently much shorter than `G`, the corrections will be large and frequent, potentially causing `nextDispatchR` to oscillate. If actual service times are consistently much longer than `G`, the corrections will be large in the other direction.\n\n3. **Anti-windup effectiveness:** The anti-windup bound (`nextDispatchR \u2265 arrivalR`) is most effective when `G` is close to the actual service time. If `G` is much larger than actual service times, the retroactive correction will frequently push `nextDispatchR` below `arrivalR`, triggering the anti-windup bound and effectively resetting the queue's virtual time to the arrival time of its oldest request.\n\nThe value `G = 3ms` was chosen empirically as a reasonable estimate for typical apiserver request latency. It is not configurable.\n\n### 14.6 Borrowing: Efficiency vs. Isolation\n\nThe borrowing mechanism (Section 10) allows priority levels to use more than their nominal allocation when other levels are underutilized. This improves overall server efficiency but reduces isolation between priority levels.\n\n**The smoothing tradeoff:** The exponential smoothing with coefficient `0.977` (time constant ~7 minutes) means that a priority level that was heavily loaded 5 minutes ago will still be allocated extra capacity today, even if its current demand is low. This prevents thrashing (rapidly oscillating allocations) but means that a sudden burst from a low-priority level may not be accommodated quickly if a high-priority level recently had high demand.\n\n**The `minCL` guarantee:** Even when borrowing is active, each level is guaranteed at least `minCL` seats. This ensures that a level cannot be completely starved by borrowing, even if its smoothed demand is very low.\n\n**Exempt levels:** Exempt priority levels consume from the server's total concurrency limit but do not participate in the borrowing algorithm. Their consumption is subtracted from `remainingServerCL` before the borrowing computation, reducing the pool available to non-exempt levels.\n\n### 14.7 Configuration Sensitivity\n\n| Parameter | Effect of Increasing | Effect of Decreasing |\n|-----------|---------------------|---------------------|\n| `DesiredNumQueues` | Better isolation, more memory, slower dispatch loop | Worse isolation, less memory, faster dispatch loop |\n| `HandSize` | Better isolation, more entropy bits needed, slower enqueue | Worse isolation, less entropy needed, faster enqueue |\n| `QueueLengthLimit` | More buffering, higher latency under load, more memory | Less buffering, more rejections under load |\n| `nominalConcurrencyShares` | Higher nominal allocation | Lower nominal allocation |\n| `lendablePercent` | More capacity available to borrow, less guaranteed minimum | Less capacity available to borrow, higher guaranteed minimum |\n| `borrowingLimitPercent` | Can borrow more, potentially starving other levels | Can borrow less, more predictable behavior |\n| `G (estimatedServiceDuration)` | Not configurable; fixed at 3ms | \u2014 |\n\n---\n\n## 15. Configuration Reference\n\n### 15.1 QueuingConfig\n\n```go\ntype QueuingConfig struct {\n    Name             string  // identifier for logging and metrics\n    DesiredNumQueues int     // number of queues; 0 = concurrency-limit only; <0 = exempt\n    QueueLengthLimit int     // max requests waiting per queue\n    HandSize         int     // shuffle sharding hand size\n}\n```\n\n**Constraints:**\n- `1 \u2264 HandSize \u2264 DesiredNumQueues \u2264 2^26`\n- `ceil(log2(DesiredNumQueues) * HandSize) \u2264 60` (entropy constraint)\n\n### 15.2 DispatchingConfig\n\n```go\ntype DispatchingConfig struct {\n    ConcurrencyLimit       int  // max seats in use simultaneously\n    ConcurrencyDenominator int  // denominator for ratio metrics (= ConcurrencyLimit when > 0)\n}\n```\n\n### 15.3 WorkEstimatorConfig\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimatorConfig struct {\n    MinimumSeats              uint64        // minimum seats for any request (default 1)\n    MaximumListSeatsLimit     uint64        // cap on list request seats\n    MaximumMutatingSeatsLimit uint64        // cap on mutating request seats\n    WatchesPerSeat            float64       // watches per seat for mutating estimator\n    Enabled                   bool          // enable mutating work estimator\n    // ... additional latency parameters\n}\n```\n\n### 15.4 Two-Phase Construction\n\nQueueSet creation and reconfiguration use a two-phase protocol to allow validation before commitment:\n\n```go\n// Phase 1: validate QueuingConfig, create Dealer\ncompleter, err := factory.BeginConstruction(qCfg, reqsGaugePair, execSeatsGauge, seatDemandGauge)\nif err != nil {\n    return err  // invalid config (e.g., entropy constraint violated)\n}\n\n// Phase 2: apply DispatchingConfig, return QueueSet\nqs := completer.Complete(dCfg)\n```\n\nFor reconfiguration of an existing QueueSet:\n```go\ncompleter, err := qs.BeginConfigChange(newQCfg)\nif err != nil {\n    return err\n}\nqs = completer.Complete(newDCfg)  // returns the same QueueSet object\n```\n\nThe two-phase design separates concerns: `QueuingConfig` validation (which can fail) is done before `DispatchingConfig` application (which cannot fail). This allows the APF controller to validate configuration changes before committing to a new concurrency allocation.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: Key Invariants\n\nThe following invariants are maintained throughout the QueueSet's operation:\n\n1. **Virtual time monotonicity:** `currentR` is non-decreasing (modulo epoch advancement).\n\n2. **Anti-windup:** For every non-empty queue, `queue.nextDispatchR \u2265 head(queue).arrivalR`.\n\n3. **Seat accounting:** `totSeatsInUse = \u03a3_q queue.seatsInUse` and `totSeatsWaiting = \u03a3_q \u03a3_{r in q.waiting} r.MaxSeats()`.\n\n4. **Concurrency limit:** `totSeatsInUse \u2264 dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit` at all times (except transiently during the final phase of wide requests, which is handled by the `AdditionalLatency` mechanism).\n\n5. **Decision finality:** Each request's `decision` promise is set exactly once, to either `decisionExecute` or `decisionCancel`.\n\n6. **Lock discipline:** All mutable queueSet state is accessed only while holding `qs.lock`. `decision.Get()` is called without the lock; `decision.Set()` is called with the lock.\n\n7. **Queue index consistency:** `queue.index` always equals the queue's position in `qs.queues`. This is maintained by `removeQueueAndUpdateIndexes` when queues are removed.\n\n8. **Epoch safety:** After epoch advancement, all R values (currentR, nextDispatchR, arrivalR) are decremented by the same `rDecrement`, preserving all relative orderings and differences.\n",
